  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app',

I'm Kidding</i>, Degeneres' first book in eight years, brings us up to date about the life of a kindhearted woman who bowed out of <i>American Idol</i> because she didn't want to be mean.               <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4632071-lora?shelf=lib-read">lib-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4632071-lora?shelf=nonfiction">nonfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4632071-lora?shelf=lib-audiobooks">lib-audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer288308941" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11571286680977118360"><b>Note: This is a review of the audio edition.</b><br/><br/>I love Ellen Degeneres. Seriously, I'm <i>not</i> kidding. I know what you're thinking: you can't truly love someone whom you've never met and probably never will. But I truly love her in the way you love someone — or something — that you know with your whole heart is making the world a better place to live. And I am positive of this fact when it comes to this woman.<br/>After a hard day, her humor and generosity and overall love for people and life are a balm on </span>
  <span id="freeText11571286680977118360" style="display:none"><b>Note: This is a review of the audio edition.</b><br /><br />I love Ellen Degeneres. Seriously, I'm <i>not</i> kidding. I know what you're thinking: you can't truly love someone whom you've never met and probably never will. But I truly love her in the way you love someone — or something — that you know with your whole heart is making the world a better place to live. And I am positive of this fact when it comes to this woman.<br />After a hard day, her humor and generosity and overall love for people and life are a balm on the world's aches. This woman makes each day better for countless people just by being herself. Did you know that scientists have proven that laughter can increase your lifespan and even help you feel and look better?<br />This isn't to mention all of the people she's helped through her show. Cars, houses, miscellaneous gifts, money — all given to people who're probably much better off after having received these various gifts.<br /><br />My library has shelved this book in the biography section, but in case there is any one wondering, let me be clear: This is <i>not</i> an autobio.<br />And although I laughed many, many times while listening to Ellen's words read in her own narration, I have to admit that a good deal of this book is, truly, just a bunch of babble.<br /><br />At times, Ellen manages to mix philosophy and deep thoughts with spontaneous humor expertly:<br /><br /><b><i>There are very few things that wow us anymore. A child will see something as simple as a garage door opening and it's literally all they will talk about for weeks. As an adult, we will see a human person ride a bike, catapult over eighteen cars that are on fire, land on a skateboard, slid down a ramp, and end up in the backseat of a taxi, and be like,</i>"Yeah, that was all right. But did you see the guy who pogo sticked over thirty-eight grandmothers?" <i>I'm not saying we need to live like babies in every way. I mean, sure, it would be great to get carried around in a papoose. Who wouldn't want that? But I am glad I'm potty trained and I'm not always trying to eat my feet like babies do. I just wish we could hold on to that sense of wonder because sometimes we don't notice some of the most incredible things in the world. We walk by beautiful flowers and trees every day without looking at them. We rush through our day without even saying hi to most of the people we see. We take a lot for granted, and I think that's why some people say it's better to live each day as our last. That way we might start appreciating more things around us. Either that or we would immediately quit our jobs to go live in a yurt.</i></b><br /><br />. . . and I love that. <i>But</i> — there were times when it leaned a bit too much on the babble side and I was thankful for having picked up the audio; if I hadn't, this book probably would've ended up unfinished.<br /><br />In a summary, I enjoyed <i>Seriously . . . I'm kidding.</i> I didn't love it like I do the lady who wrote it, but I enjoyed it nonetheless.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11571286680977118360" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer218630089" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8391761261389706567">When I was a little girl, my grandfather once told me that when he spoke in front of a group, he often began with, "I know most people start their speeches with jokes, but I don't know any, so let's all think of our favorite joke and laugh." This book reminded me a lot of that joke. <br/><br/>While I don't watch Ellen's talk show, I do really like her and have read her other books. This one seems... gratuitous. One chapter is made up entirely of her making sounds. As in, mememememeeme. Or, bwabwabwa. A fe</span>
  <span id="freeText8391761261389706567" style="display:none">When I was a little girl, my grandfather once told me that when he spoke in front of a group, he often began with, "I know most people start their speeches with jokes, but I don't know any, so let's all think of our favorite joke and laugh." This book reminded me a lot of that joke. <br /><br />While I don't watch Ellen's talk show, I do really like her and have read her other books. This one seems... gratuitous. One chapter is made up entirely of her making sounds. As in, mememememeeme. Or, bwabwabwa. A few chapters are short, fictional stories, similar to: "A woman walks down the beach, and sees the waves. Hello, waves. END." Several are meandering thoughts, a la her Nemo character. Another handful of chapters are set in a faux meditation class, where she pretends to be your meditation teacher but only leads to you picking out the bothersome parts of your session. Even she seems to realize it's sort of bland - each chapter begins with her exaggerating the number (chapter TENNNNNN! chapter tweeeeenty FIVE!), then launching into the text in a sort of bored voice. <br /><br />If you're looking for interesting or humorous commentary on the world, on issues, on her life, this book is not for you. If you need to kill 10 minutes at the bus stop each day, this could work. <br /><br />Chapters I've listened to since last posting: <br />Ellen ate an apple. (Crunch, crunch. That's it.)<br />A fake dream.<br />Ellen saying, "Yes, no, yes. Yes, no."</span>

<div id="review_3011001013" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3011001013" />
    <a title="exploraDora" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36234199-exploradora"><img alt="exploraDora" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525708467p2/36234199.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3011001013?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="exploraDora" class="user" itemprop="url" name="exploraDora" href="/user/show/36234199-exploradora">exploraDora</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36234199-exploradora?shelf=humour">humour</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36234199-exploradora?shelf=nonfiction">nonfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36234199-exploradora?shelf=autobiography">autobiography</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36234199-exploradora?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3011001013" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6252152525636488389"><br/><b>***2 stars***</b><br/><br/>I would like to start off by saying that I like Ellen a lot. That's why I decided to read one of her books. She's fun and seems like a genuinely lovely person. <b>UPDATE:</b> Lately, I keep hearing that she's actually not that great in real life?! Idk what to think..<br/><br/>Anyway<br/><br/>While listening to this, I felt like I was being messed with or mocked. <br/>The audiobook is read by Ellen herself, which was nice. But 90 percent of the time I felt like she was just... rambling. To give you an example: for </span>
  <span id="freeText6252152525636488389" style="display:none"><br><b>***2 stars***</b><br><br>I would like to start off by saying that I like Ellen a lot. That's why I decided to read one of her books. She's fun and seems like a genuinely lovely person. <b>UPDATE:</b> Lately, I keep hearing that she's actually not that great in real life?! Idk what to think..<br><br>Anyway<br><br>While listening to this, I felt like I was being messed with or mocked. <br>The audiobook is read by Ellen herself, which was nice. But 90 percent of the time I felt like she was just... rambling. To give you an example: for a whole minute, she talks about a word she wrote down in some notes and wonders what it says. From there she basically just says a bunch of random words with no meaning whatsoever, then asks herself if it even is her handwriting. All this to eventually end up eating an apple :/ So I listened to Ellen eat an apple for 28 seconds. WHAT KIND OF JOKE IS THIS?<br><br>I know that it's comedy and that it's all supposed to be taken with a grain of salt, I just couldn't help but roll my eyes and even cringe for the most part. It felt like she had no idea what to write in this book, so she just talks about meaningless things to get down to a certain word count. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1571008603i/28289200._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height='380"' alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>You know?<br><br>Maybe I'm not getting it.<br>Maybe it's just not my type of humor. Idk, but I don't think this is a very good book.<br><br>Sorry, Ellen. I still like you and your show, though!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6252152525636488389" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1880060541" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1880060541" />
    <a title="Nat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23381142-nat"><img alt="Nat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588309995p2/23381142.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1880060541?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nat" href="/user/show/23381142-nat">Nat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23381142-nat?shelf=nonfiction">nonfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23381142-nat?shelf=memoir">memoir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23381142-nat?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23381142-nat?shelf=essays">essays</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1880060541" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18359020749931563115"><i>“It always helps to think about other people instead of ourselves.”</i><br/><br/>I picked up this audiobook in hopes of it lifting up my spirits while I had a cold. And for the first two (out of three) hours it did its job. I laughed heartily while getting to forget for a minute that I was feeling awful. And two passages in particular really stayed with me.<br/><br/>One for being witty: <i>“Do things that make you happy within the confines of the legal system.”</i><br/><br/>And the other for being relatable: <i>“Leaning forward in your ch</i></span>
  <span id="freeText18359020749931563115" style="display:none"><i>“It always helps to think about other people instead of ourselves.”</i><br><br>I picked up this audiobook in hopes of it lifting up my spirits while I had a cold. And for the first two (out of three) hours it did its job. I laughed heartily while getting to forget for a minute that I was feeling awful. And two passages in particular really stayed with me.<br><br>One for being witty: <i>“Do things that make you happy within the confines of the legal system.”</i><br><br>And the other for being relatable: <i>“Leaning forward in your chair when someone is trying to squeeze behind you isn't enough. You also have to move the chair.”</i><br><br><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1485157610ra/21788683.gif" width="420" height="235" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>There's quite a few things I was to discuss, so let's start with the things I enjoyed:<br><br>• The comedic timing.<br>• The author sharing details and the behind the scenes of her talk show, interviewing guests and how she needs to keep talking and talking and talking for hours.<br>• how the audiobook had certain chapters that got background noises, such as beach waves, rain drops, casino noises...<br>• DeGeneres repeatedly mentioning her want for a <i>Nemo</i> sequel.<br>• when she talked about the environment, coming out, being happy, veganism, and becoming a cover girl.<br><br>But I feel like everything that was important was glossed over. Meanwhile, the topics that contributed nothing more than to pass the time were elaborated on more than necessary… <br>Real talk: you can quit listening after two hours because nothing meaningful is said after. We have chapters about:<br><br>• math equations and counting to “help” the listeners fall asleep.<br>• making up a dream where the listener is a reptile...<br>• deciding to eat an apple instead of reading the chapter about text abbreviations… really?!<br>• making strange noises with her mouth just for the audio listeners... I wish I were kidding, but I can't make this shit up. I had to put the volume on low so my mom wouldn’t think I was actually listening to someone making weird noises in an audiobook.<br>• also, on a totally separate note, I kind of hated how the author kept bashing social media and using the phrase “technology is destroying our social skills.” To quote <a href="https://www.techdirt.com/articles/20140804/20514528111/technology-doesnt-make-us-less-social-it-just-changes-way-we-socialize.shtml" rel="nofollow noopener">this article</a>, technology doesn't make us less social; it just changes the way we socialise. And I'd recommend watching <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=IH4sdD5i0uM" rel="nofollow noopener">this brilliant episode</a> from the show <i>Black-ish</i> discuss this topic as well.<br>• And most importantly, her white privilege kept showing throughout without being examined...<br><br>Simply put, a lot of chapters felt like filler, which towards the end really got on my nerves. The more nonsense was said, the more fuming I got. And to be honest, this book doesn't really contribute anything new or exiting about DeGeneres. If you didn’t read <b>Seriously... I'm Kidding</b>, you would know the same amount about the author by watching the talkshow.<br><br>I personally haven't watched <i>The Ellen Show</i> in awhile, so the only thing that compelled me to pick this up was my feeling ill and desperately wanting to distract myself of it. So I appreciate this read more for making me feel a little better rather than for its content.<br><br><b>2.5/5 stars</b><br><br><em><em>Note: I'm an Amazon Affiliate. If you're interested in buying</em> </em><strong>Seriously... I'm Kidding</strong><em>
  <em>, just click on the image below to go through my link. I'll make a small commission!</em>
</em><br><a href="https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0446585041/ref=as_li_tl?ie=UTF8&amp;camp=1789&amp;creative=9325&amp;creativeASIN=0446585041&amp;linkCode=as2&amp;tag=natalie013-20&amp;linkId=7c6d74fecef8cfb23a2c63da55ee8a17" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1485157536i/21788670.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">This review and more can be found on my blog.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="18359020749931563115" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_357477084" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/357477084" />
    <a title="Crystal Starr Light" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3990525-crystal-starr-light"><img alt="Crystal Starr Light" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573066911p2/3990525.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/357477084?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Crystal Starr Light" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Crystal Starr Light" href="/user/show/3990525-crystal-starr-light">Crystal Starr Light</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781609410414" href="/book/show/11276785-seriously-i-m-kidding">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=biography">biography</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=editor-wanted">editor-wanted</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer357477084" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2730953313889832702">You wanna read/listen to an amusing little time waster and you like Ellen DeGeneres' style of humor? This is your book. However, don't go into this expecting anything really substantial. Some chapters are a couple of words, maybe a sentence long. And while I adored some of the stories and was uplifted by the encouraging tone, that is where my biggest complaint is.<br/><br/>I listened to this in 3 hours. This is the absolute shortest audiobook I've ever listened to--and this goes for almost $30 retail. You</span>
  <span id="freeText2730953313889832702" style="display:none">You wanna read/listen to an amusing little time waster and you like Ellen DeGeneres' style of humor? This is your book. However, don't go into this expecting anything really substantial. Some chapters are a couple of words, maybe a sentence long. And while I adored some of the stories and was uplifted by the encouraging tone, that is where my biggest complaint is.<br /><br />I listened to this in 3 hours. This is the absolute shortest audiobook I've ever listened to--and this goes for almost $30 retail. You could go to the movie theater for nearly 3 hours and pay less--and probably have just as good or a better time.<br /><br />Of course, that probably sounds like I hated the book. Not true. Ellen is funny, in her own way, and she really is a good narrator. I cracked a smile quite a few times and laughed a few others (and I'm not a big one to laugh while reading or listening to a book). Ellen also doesn't just make jokes; she's inspiring and uplifting, encouraging meditation, recycling, decluttering, spending time with family, getting regular health check-ups, and more.<br /><br />But I'll admit, after awhile it got old. There are only so many uplifting messages I can take before it feels like I'm being lectured to--and there is nothing worse than to have someone tell you the life you're living (with which you are quite content and are not harming anyone) isn't nearly as good as X's. Some jokes however didn't do it for me--such as her joke on the 80% of graduates that are moving back with their parents because they are moochers (no, not all of them are, it's the lack of jobs). I also don't get the joke of hearing Ellen say things like "mememememeee". ("Really? I paid $30 to hear Ellen say 'mememememe'"?)<br /><br />As for talking about her own life--I know a lot has happened in Ellen's life. I know this from Wiki and the news, certainly not from this book. Sure, Ellen talks a bit about American Idol and her talk show and mentions Portia in passing. But those references are few and far between, so keep your eyes and ears open or you are bound to miss it.<br /><br />All in all, while there are some really good parts, a lot of the 3 hours just felt like filler. To give a comparison, at the end of Tina Fey's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9418327.Bossypants" title="Bossypants by Tina Fey" rel="nofollow noopener">Bossypants</a>, I felt I had learned a great deal about Fey and left wanting to watch 30 Rock. After listening to this, I felt like I had finished eating cotton candy and was hungry for some real food. I was super glad I had checked this out at the library; I would have felt cheated for spending retail price on it.<br /><br />My recommendation is: check this out from your library, see if you like it before spending nearly $30 on the audiobook or hardcover. Or you are likely to be VERY disappointed.<br /><br />And because this book was so terribly short, I'll do the same and keep this review short too.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2730953313889832702" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Kelli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4146551-kelli"><img alt="Kelli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413330332p2/4146551.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1600476678?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1600476678" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1724441518323867340">Seriously...I'm bored. And shocked. This audio is not well read by the author (how is that even possible?). There is little affect, there are no pauses, and it seemed like even she was racing to get to the end. The content was all over the place. I really like Ellen and I've always found her funny. I guess her humor doesn't translate well to books for me. Reading it for audio, it didn't seem like she found it funny, either. Sadly, 1 star.</span>

For example: People who are late for dinner parties (it's rude and may lead to the hosts being in their pajamas by the time dinner ends).<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1559858216i/27629061._SY540_.jpg' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Being a Cover Girl model - it's hard being beautiful.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1559858216i/27629062.jpg' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Coming out as gay (she's </span>
  <span id="freeText8233660447653949760" style="display:none"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1559858216i/27629060.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Ellen DeGeneres</b><br><br>I listened to the audio version of this book and it's a lot like watching Ellen talk on her television show - lots of casual, humorous observations about everyday life. <br><br>Ellen riffs on a wide variety of random topics, seemingly whatever pops into her head at the moment. LOL); and much more.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1559858216i/27629063.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Finding Dory - the sequel to Finding Nemo</b><br><br>My favorite chapter is Ellen's satirical, funny letter to the security department of a mall where - it's been suggested - she broke a vase in a Pottery Barn store. Her explanation of how this happened - and how it's not her fault - is hilarious. A tip: if you're in a mall, don't swipe a security guard's segway, "accidently" ride it all over the mall, try to return it to a dumpster out back, fall asleep on a sofa in Pottery barn, become startled awake, fall off, and dislodge cushions that fly off to break a vase. And that's not even the half of it.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1559858216i/27629064._SX540_.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This is a light, fun book, and the audio version is perfect for doing chores or listening to in the car.<br><br>You can follow my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://reviewsbybarbsaffer.blogspot.com/">http://reviewsbybarbsaffer.blogspot.com/</a></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason Koivu" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason Koivu" href="/user/show/1742824-jason-koivu">Jason Koivu</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1742824-jason-koivu?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1742824-jason-koivu?shelf=autobiography">autobiography</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1802093816" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2982323478722256022"><b>5 GLORIOUS STARS!!!</b> is what I wanted to give <i>Seriously...I'm Kidding</i> when I first picked it up. The peace and kindness message is great, but this lacks the funny far too much for an autobio from a comedian. <br/><br/>I love Ellen DeGeneres. Wait, let me back up. I love the idea of Ellen DeGeneres. I really like her show. Her stand-up...meh. Unfortunately, this book is more like her stand-up. This very quick read (actually, I listened to her read it and it was only 3 cds) is sprinkled with her silly titter</span>
  <span id="freeText2982323478722256022" style="display:none"><b>5 GLORIOUS STARS!!!</b> is what I wanted to give <i>Seriously...I'm Kidding</i> when I first picked it up. The peace and kindness message is great, but this lacks the funny far too much for an autobio from a comedian. <br /><br />I love Ellen DeGeneres. Wait, let me back up. I love the idea of Ellen DeGeneres. I really like her show. Her stand-up...meh. Unfortunately, this book is more like her stand-up. This very quick read (actually, I listened to her read it and it was only 3 cds) is sprinkled with her silly titter-inducing jokey things and the rest is fluff. There are whole chapters of filler. There are sections of her making nonsensical noises, her eating, and her saying nothing. Literally intentional silence. As if that wasn't bad enough, there's a whole bit about dreams. I would've preferred more silence.<br /><br />I'd say about halfway through I thought <i>Seriously...I'm Kidding</i> deserved about 3 stars, but the latter half took a complete nose-dive. Very boring, tedious even. That's sad. I had high hopes. I guess I'll go back to checking out Youtube clips of her show. Those crack me up.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/238571396?book_show_action=true">Nov 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Davytron" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Davytron" href="/user/show/5662520-davytron">Davytron</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">people who have an hour to spend in a book store</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5662520-davytron?shelf=bioautobiomemoir">bioautobiomemoir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5662520-davytron?shelf=edit-me">edit-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5662520-davytron?shelf=wtf">wtf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5662520-davytron?shelf=the-worst">the-worst</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer238571396" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14123302168326837736">Update: The ire against Ellen at the moment has brought people to this review, somehow. I didn't like Ellen then and I don't like her now - honestly I didn't think it took x-ray vision to see through her then (she has always belittled and treated others with contempt) but I am glad people are coming around. Too bad she's already made millions so she doesn't even have to care. <br/><br/>As expected, this book was a joke. This thirty dollar waste of time and money <b>should-have-been-a-free-blog/twitter-post</b> i</span>
  <span id="freeText14123302168326837736" style="display:none">Update: The ire against Ellen at the moment has brought people to this review, somehow. I didn't like Ellen then and I don't like her now - honestly I didn't think it took x-ray vision to see through her then (she has always belittled and treated others with contempt) but I am glad people are coming around. Too bad she's already made millions so she doesn't even have to care. <br /><br />As expected, this book was a joke. This thirty dollar waste of time and money <b>should-have-been-a-free-blog/twitter-post</b> is an insult to Ellen's fan base. Yes, there are a few moments where I laughed out loud but that does not make up for the significant lack of cohesion or purpose behind anything Ellen wrote. It's as if she had come up with a bunch of unrelated but great one-liners and observations but didn't have anywhere to stick them in her show so she decided to unload them in a completely random fashion in an overpriced, super short book. So many of the chapters were meandering stories that had no relation to the actual point. One chapter she abruptly stopped and said "maybe I shouldn't have written this chapter" after getting off track. <br /><br />This book was seemingly Ellen's attempt at encouraging people to be happy. She tries to emphasize the importance of doing stuff, communicating, and eating right. It was particularly ridiculous when Ellen chastised society for preferring shorter, impersonal communication (e.g. twitter) and then talked about the importance of reading books. Was she talking about her own book? Because her book is the embodiment of the preference she criticizes. The chapters are at max 4 pages each with giant font and margins; any idea she presents is briefly touched upon but never elaborated or explained. I would have been happy to read this book for what it was - a brief, funny examination of the thought process of a family-friendly comedian - if the publisher hadn't tried to gauge the public by charging $30!<br /><br />If you're a fan of Ellen and desperate to read this book, just sit in the bookstore and read it for free. It will only take you an hour and you won't have supported this transparent celebrity cash grab. Real artists struggle to get their books published and this tripe was clearly published only because it's Ellen. <br /><br />Memory Index:<br />Anticipated: 0<br />Actual: 0 (literally haven't thought about this book periodt.).</span>
  <a data-text-id="14123302168326837736" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText9493992534957423747" style="display:none">As a kid I loved Ellen DeGeneres. I watched her ABC sitcom. I watched all her HBO standup specials. I just thought she was hilarious. <br /><br />Now as an adult I don't get why she's so popular. I've tried watching her talk show and I find it annoying. Maybe what I find funny is just completely different as an adult or maybe Ellen is just boring and lame.<br /><br />If you enjoy Ellen's show, then enjoy this book.<br /><br />It just wasn't for me.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/259137163?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2012</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer259137163" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7760574366185424440">I love Ellen. After listening to this audiobook I still love Ellen! Some people don't normally find her that amusing. To those people I say, "You're stupid." Just kidding. If you didn't think that was funny, then you might not like this book. But to me, it was laugh-out-loud hilarity the whole way through. A few jokes were even so funny that I kept reliving them afterwards and going around town laughing sporadically. It is probably best that I just let people think that I'm laughing at them rath</span>
  <span id="freeText7760574366185424440" style="display:none">I love Ellen. After listening to this audiobook I still love Ellen! Some people don't normally find her that amusing. To those people I say, "You're stupid." Just kidding. If you didn't think that was funny, then you might not like this book. But to me, it was laugh-out-loud hilarity the whole way through. A few jokes were even so funny that I kept reliving them afterwards and going around town laughing sporadically. It is probably best that I just let people think that I'm laughing at them rather than explaining about how I'm laughing at Ellen's joke about "getting back on the horse" where she preteded she was actually getting back on those little merry-go-round pay coin-pay horses outside of the grocery store. <br />I love Ellen and I record her show every day because it makes me happy! The best is when SHE starts laughing. I crack-up forever. I'm seriously still laughing at this time when Debra Messing was on about 5 years ago and a recorder-playing man dressed in a soldier suit started cheerfully walking by. <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=amAl29aMLqg">http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=amAl29...</a> This clip doesn't quite do it justice because it doesn't show the interruption, but maybe it will make you laugh anyway. If you've read this far then you must be a friend or just have a lot of time on your hands! :0) (I kinda went off on a tangent!)</span>
  <a data-text-id="7760574366185424440" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/246418172" />
    <a title="Sandy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2463587-sandy"><img alt="Sandy" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/246418172?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandy" href="/user/show/2463587-sandy">Sandy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer246418172" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15961323362576479415">Seriously...I'm Kidding by Ellen DeGeneres is a goofy, cute, and at-times comical book. Each chapter/section is random and does not make sense at some parts. If you like Ellen's brand of humour then this is a nice escape for a few hours. It's also a very quick read meant to pass the time. The book is supposed to highlight what's going on in Ellen's life but I'm able to pick out very little of what I think are actually real slices of her life when the rest is just meant to amuse and distract the </span>
  <span id="freeText15961323362576479415" style="display:none">Seriously...I'm Kidding by Ellen DeGeneres is a goofy, cute, and at-times comical book. Each chapter/section is random and does not make sense at some parts. If you like Ellen's brand of humour then this is a nice escape for a few hours. It's also a very quick read meant to pass the time. The book is supposed to highlight what's going on in Ellen's life but I'm able to pick out very little of what I think are actually real slices of her life when the rest is just meant to amuse and distract the reader.<br /><br />This is not a memoir, a biography, or a serious book of any genre or nature. I'm not sure you can even classify it as nonfiction. I'm not sure if you're even supposed to say it's for adults or for children, or even teens. But if you want a break from something serious or heavy then pick up this book (I recommend borrowing from your local public library like I did) for you to focus on. I'm also disappointed because I expected something deeper/real from Ellen but she engages you in anything but her life, aside from minor tidbits that barely scratch the surface. The rest are just her jokes and ramblings.</span>

          </span>

My favorite standard Ellen jokes are when she talks about not wearing pants or drinking too much wine.<br/><br/>I guess my expectations were a little off when I read this.   <span id="freeText10050978310753456762" style="display:none">I only snickered a couple times while reading this. I wanted to laugh out loud! My favorite standard Ellen jokes are when she talks about not wearing pants or drinking too much wine.<br /><br />I guess my expectations were a little off when I read this. I wanted to hear jokes or more about Ellen's life, but instead, I got chapters where she encouraged me to recycle, to be happy, and to meditate. She sounded an awful lot like Oprah. Not really. Ellen doesn't take herself too seriously. (See the title.) She even took a few jabs at Oprah in the book, which made me laugh.<br /><br />In one chapter, Ellen mentions a time when Portia thought she discovered a new species of animal, but it just turned out to be a javelina. Javelina? I live in Oklahoma. I've never heard of a javelina! I had to get out of my comfy chair and walk over to my laptop and find a picture of a javelina on Google. I really would have appreciated a picture of a javelina in the book. It wouldn't even have to be the SPECIFIC javelina that Portia and Ellen saw. It could just be a stock photo. Other pictures from Ellen's stories would have been welcomed as well. She could have also added funny captions below each picture.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15407084735655628281">⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️ / 5<br/><br/>I really don't understand why there are so many poor reviews for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11230081.Seriously____I_m_Kidding' title='Seriously... I'm Kidding by Ellen DeGeneres' rel='nofollow noopener'>Seriously... I'm Kidding</a> by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/40648.Ellen_DeGeneres' title='Ellen DeGeneres' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ellen DeGeneres</a>, this was such a good little audiobook!<br/><br/>There isn't anything too incredibly serious in <i>Seriously... I'm Kidding</i>, which I guess was to be expected. In true Ellen fashion this short audiobook was full of fun sound effects and lots of jokes. She didn't talk too much about her life in general so I am hesitant to call this book a memoir or autobiography, I might have to read her oth</span>
  <span id="freeText15407084735655628281" style="display:none">⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️ / 5<br /><br />I really don't understand why there are so many poor reviews for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11230081.Seriously____I_m_Kidding" title="Seriously... I'm Kidding by Ellen DeGeneres" rel="nofollow noopener">Seriously... I'm Kidding</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/40648.Ellen_DeGeneres" title="Ellen DeGeneres" rel="nofollow noopener">Ellen DeGeneres</a>, this was such a good little audiobook!<br /><br />There isn't anything too incredibly serious in <i>Seriously... I'm Kidding</i>, which I guess was to be expected. In true Ellen fashion this short audiobook was full of fun sound effects and lots of jokes. She didn't talk too much about her life in general so I am hesitant to call this book a memoir or autobiography, I might have to read her other books for that. I know the synopsis says the intent of this book is to bring everyone up to date on her life from her book eight years prior, but I found there to be more comedy than substance about her life. That being said, she did mention that she has a record label and got chosen as a CoverGirl multiple times. I am sure it was meant for comedic effect that she said it so many times, but I did think it was a little much. <br /><br /><b>Final Thought:</b> <i>Seriously... I'm Kidding</i> is super short at only 3 hours and 6 minutes so I am going to keep my review short and sweet as well. I absolutely adore Ellen, and I think for the length this book was, it was really good. It definitely makes me want to listen to her other books as well, and if you love Ellen you will hopefully enjoy this book as much as I did! </span>
  <a data-text-id="15407084735655628281" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <a href="/user/show/3990525-crystal-starr-light">Crystal Starr Light</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1633094276" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10874120291149087699"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463008324ra/19072060.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463008324ra/19072061.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463008324ra/19072062.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>---<br/>3.5 stars<br/><br/>Had read one of Ellen's books years ago and thought it was just 'okay.' It wasn't that I didn't like it, it just seemed her great personality and humor didn't translate as well to paper (I think I am in the minority there). I meant to read her other book but forgot until I saw this book of hers came out, but for some reason never got around to either one.<br/><br/>In my humble opinion, this is a better way to read Ellen's books.<br/><br/>Another case of 'Why not? Let's go for it :)'<br/><br/>Ellen's narration was</span>
  <span id="freeText10874120291149087699" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463008324ra/19072060.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463008324ra/19072061.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463008324ra/19072062.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>---<br>3.5 stars<br><br>Had read one of Ellen's books years ago and thought it was just 'okay.' It wasn't that I didn't like it, it just seemed her great personality and humor didn't translate as well to paper (I think I am in the minority there). I meant to read her other book but forgot until I saw this book of hers came out, but for some reason never got around to either one.<br><br>In my humble opinion, this is a better way to read Ellen's books.<br><br>Another case of 'Why not? Let's go for it :)'<br><br>Ellen's narration was a smidge awkward in the beginning but hit its stride not long after. There were times when my inner cynic popped up but overall this was alot of fun. The "pointless" chapters were some of my favorites :).<br><br><i>“Beauty is about being comfortable in your own skin. It's about knowing and accepting who you are.” <br><br>“True beauty is not related to what color your hair is or what color your eyes are. True beauty is about who you are as a human being, your principles, your moral compass.” <br><br>“What’s not so great is that all this technology is destroying our social skills. Not only have we given up on writing letters to each other, we barely even talk to each other. People have become so accustomed to texting that they’re actually startled when the phone rings. It’s like we suddenly all have Batphones. If it rings, there must be danger. <br><br>Now we answer, “What happened? Is someone tied up in the old sawmill?”<br><br>“No, it’s Becky. I just called to say hi.”<br><br>“Well you scared me half to death. You can’t just pick up the phone and try to talk to me like that. Don’t the tips of your fingers work?”<br><br>“I'm just saying we can all work on our manners. We can say please and thank you. We can be punctual. We can just be nicer to one another. It's something we have in our power to do. It reminds me of that Margaret Mead quote: "Never doubt that a small group of thoughtful, committed citizens can change the world. Indeed, it's the only thing that ever has.” </i><br>----<br><br>I did agree with Ellen on alot of things in here but the jokes about the college kids, maybe she didn't mean anything by it but I didn't find that one funny in the slightest.<br><br>This more amusing than laugh-out-loud funny, it's a bit all over the place but that's half the charm really :).<br><br>One of the shortest audiobooks I've read but it did lift my mood so mission accomplished? Would recommend, especially if you are a fan of Ellen, but I would recommend borrowing it from the library or a friend before you commit to buying it.<br><br>Ellen is one of the people I want to adopt as friend/family... hopefully will meet her one day *crosses fingers*<br><br>Review Spotlight:<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/357477084/" rel="nofollow noopener">Crystal's review</a></span>

<div id="review_1922712396" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1922712396" />
    <a title="Bonnie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5136858-bonnie"><img alt="Bonnie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604440764p2/5136858.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1922712396?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bonnie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bonnie" href="/user/show/5136858-bonnie">Bonnie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781609410414" href="/book/show/11276785-seriously-i-m-kidding">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Bonnie by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/23397406-dani">Dani</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5136858-bonnie?shelf=non-fiction-memoirs-and-bios">non-fiction-memoirs-and-bios</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5136858-bonnie?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5136858-bonnie?shelf=funny-ha-ha">funny-ha-ha</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5136858-bonnie?shelf=library-audio">library-audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1922712396" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6372093745623041210"><b>
  <i>“So be who you really are. Embrace who you are. Literally. Hug yourself. Accept who you are. Unless you’re a serial killer.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>I was having a pretty bad day when I started this. There was a lot of driving involved that I wasn’t looking forward to and an unexpected blizzard to boot. I always like a good audiobook to keep me company I just didn’t think anything was going to be able to get me out of the funk I was in — but I underestimated Ellen.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1488606631ra/22135244.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I’m Kidding…Seriously aims at being a light-hearted </span>
  <span id="freeText6372093745623041210" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>“So be who you really are. Embrace who you are. Literally. Hug yourself. Accept who you are. Unless you’re a serial killer.”</i>
</b><br><br>I was having a pretty bad day when I started this. There was a lot of driving involved that I wasn’t looking forward to and an unexpected blizzard to boot. I always like a good audiobook to keep me company I just didn’t think anything was going to be able to get me out of the funk I was in — but I underestimated Ellen.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1488606631ra/22135244.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I’m Kidding…Seriously aims at being a light-hearted advice manual with the main goal of just making you smile. She takes digs at her fellow celebrities and their hilarious lifestyles but becomes quickly somber when discussing the importance of being true to yourself and accepting who you are as a person. This isn’t your typical inspirational celebrity memoir on how to make it big in Hollywood but rather reads like an internal monologue with the author herself. If you’re an audiobook lover, do yourself a favor and listen to this one because Ellen’s tone and delivery make this all the more enjoyable an experience. If you’re a fan of her stand-up comedy routines, you’ll find much to laugh about in this. I know I did.<br><br><b>
  <i>‘I feel bad for people December birthdays […] It’s not fair and I have a message for parents out there. Don’t do that to your kids. Plan your love. I’m not great at baby math, so I’m just gonna say in the early part of the year, maybe January until March, stay away from each other. It’s not gonna be easy. Those are winter months and you’re going to want to stay warm. But unfortunately one of you is going to have to sleep in a tent in the backyard.’</i>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="6372093745623041210" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1/5Q+PuRbb5zaQz88qBhMImTlUYscoAJrJl47xtZC576GWXkGh3iwTsaO6KQFSIwEaVaBSqkRs8W3eBKdRNR8A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('DRULlb1QLFFFJeMsbA5srriSEwRmw8i/EvwgrfGOhDcg8j6JXNyjLg1W1HIOuy+uIKTcR2AVDnmouLgIn8TeWQ==')})
  }
//]]>

Now, Amy Schumer has written a refreshingly candid and uproariously funny collection of (extremely) personal and observational essays. \n\nIn The Girl with the Lower Back Tattoo, Amy mines her past for stories about her teenage years, her family, relationships, and sex and shares the experiences that have shaped who she is - a woman with the courage to bare her soul to stand up for what she believes in, all while making us laugh.\n\nRanging from the raucous to the romantic, the heartfelt to the harrowing, this highly entertaining and universally appealing collection is the literary equivalent of a night out with your best friends - an unforgettable and fun adventure that you wish could last forever. Whether she\'s experiencing lust-at-first-sight while in the airport security line, sharing her own views on love and marriage, admitting to being an introvert, or discovering her cross-fit <span id="freeTextContainer173817165218648860">Ellen Lee DeGeneres is an American stand-up comedian, actress, and currently the Emmy Award-winning host of the syndicated talk show The Ellen DeGeneres Show.<br/><br/>She has hosted both the Academy Awards and the Primetime Emmys. As a film actress, she starred in <i>Mr. Wrong</i>, appeared in <i>Edtv</i> and <i>The Love Letter</i>, and provided the voice of "Dory" in the Pixar animated hit film <i>Finding Nemo</i>. She also starred </span>
  <span id="freeText173817165218648860" style="display:none">Ellen Lee DeGeneres is an American stand-up comedian, actress, and currently the Emmy Award-winning host of the syndicated talk show The Ellen DeGeneres Show.<br /><br />She has hosted both the Academy Awards and the Primetime Emmys. As a film actress, she starred in <i>Mr. Wrong</i>, appeared in <i>Edtv</i> and <i>The Love Letter</i>, and provided the voice of "Dory" in the Pixar animated hit film <i>Finding Nemo</i>. She also starred in two television sitcoms, <i>The Ellen Show</i> from 2001 to 2002 and <i>Ellen</i> from 1994 to 1998. In 1997 during the fourth season of Ellen, she "came out" publicly as a lesbian in an appearance on <i>The Oprah Winfrey Show</i>. Shortly afterwards, her character Ellen Morgan also came out and the series went on to explore various LGBT issues as well as the "coming out" process.<br /><br />Ellen is married to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3405767.Portia_de_Rossi" title="Portia de Rossi" rel="nofollow noopener">Portia de Rossi</a>.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="173817165218648860" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
